EG12261	b3534	3695233	3695985	EG12261-MONOMER	ECK3519	EG12261	yhjQ	bcsQ	In the commensal cellulose-producing <i>E. coli</i> strain 1094, BcsQ is required for cellulose production and localizes to the cell poles |CITS: [19400787]|.  

In <i>E. coli</i> K-12 strains such as W3110 and MG1655, a "domesticating SNP" consists of a point mutation that introduces a stop codon after the first 5 amino acids of the wild-type <i>bcsQ</i> ORF.  Additionally, the domesticating SNP lowers expression of both <i>bcsQ</i> and the downstream <i>bcsA</i> gene.  After repairing the SNP, the resulting "de-domesticated" W3110 derivative produces cellulose and has dramatically altered biofilm morphology.  A &Delta;<i>bcsQ</i> mutation introduced into this strain leads to loss of cellulose biosynthesis |CITS: [24097954]| (see also |CITS: [31604608]|). 

BcsQ belongs to the ParA family of ATPases which also includes MinD.  The N-terminal predicted ATP-binding domain of BcsQ (in strain 1094) is required for function, but not for the polar localization of the protein, while the C-terminal domain contributes to both localization and function in cellulose biosynthesis |CITS: [19400787]|. In the cellulose producing strain <i>E. coli</i> 1094, the inner membrane and cytosolic Bcs proteins - BcsA, BcsB, BscQ, BcsG, BcsE, BcsR and BcsF - organize in a multisubunit, stable macrocomplex; two-hybrid assays identified multiple direct interactions between the subunits and a low resolution structure has been obtained |CITS: [29234007]|.

A <i>bcsQ</i> mutant was seen to exhibit filamentous morphology, heterogeneous cell size, and a defect in chromosome partitioning |CITS: [12382054]|, but |CITS: [19400787]| was unable to reproduce these phenotypes.

BcsQ: "<b>b</b>acterial <b>c</b>ellulose <b>s</b>ynthesis"

Related review: |CITS: [26077867]|

<i>yfzA</i> was deaccessioned in ASAP in 2007.  Comment in ASAP: "yzfA (b4223) is no longer thought to be an actual gene and has been deaccessioned; this reading frame is on the opposite strand of ytfP"

Eric Neeno-Eckwall, personal communication 11/7/2018: YtfP is highly conserved among the enterobacteria, with conservation of genome context as far out as Vibrio. I looked at a couple of examples, and the coding sequence of yzfA is not conserved. It would be a pseudogene in Dickeya, and would have a long C-terminal extension in Salmonella (and is not predicted by GeneMark). A version in Escherichia albertii (87% nucleotide identity for ytfP) would require a different start codon and is also not predicted by GeneMark.
